<div id="review_2235759619" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2235759619" />
    <a title="Aliyah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41115013-aliyah"><img alt="Aliyah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567764843p2/41115013.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2235759619?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aliyah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aliyah" href="/user/show/41115013-aliyah">Aliyah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41115013-aliyah?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2235759619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17543716794703563324">Why can’t we stay in Germany? Will we ever come back? Where will we live? All those questions run through Anna’s mind. It’s 1933, and pictures of Hitler are everywhere. When he rises to power, Anna and her family are forced to leave their home behind. It is no longer safe for Jews to live in Germany. Fearing for their safety, Anna’s family move to 3 different countries in the course of a few short years. Anna must learn new languages and customs and make new friends. Each time she is finally mak</span>
  <span id="freeText17543716794703563324" style="display:none">Why can’t we stay in Germany? Will we ever come back? Where will we live? All those questions run through Anna’s mind. It’s 1933, and pictures of Hitler are everywhere. When he rises to power, Anna and her family are forced to leave their home behind. It is no longer safe for Jews to live in Germany. Fearing for their safety, Anna’s family move to 3 different countries in the course of a few short years. Anna must learn new languages and customs and make new friends. Each time she is finally making headway, she has to leave it all behind and start again. While some would say her childhood is one of difficulty, she is happy. She has the remarkable ability to find joy in the hard times. And she knows that as long as her family stay together, everything will be ok. <br />When Hitler Stole Pink Rabbit is written in a way that reflects the real dangers of the author’s own childhood while still having a lightheartedness about it. I think it is aimed at younger readers, but I still enjoyed reading it. On the surface it’s a sweet refugee story from the perspective of a little girl, but if you dig deeper you come to realize that there is so much more to it. There are underlying themes of the desire to be accepted, the strength that comes from the unity of family, and the way that various cultures are compatible with each other even when they have so many differences. <br />This book contrasts many war-time stories in that Anna is not an orphan – she always has her parents with her. Also, there isn’t lots of worry about Hitler - the book focuses more on how the family will survive as refugees. <br />I recommend When Hitler Stole Pink Rabbit for ages 8 and up and give it 3 out of 5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17543716794703563324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2962720364" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2962720364" />
    <a title="Vicki Antipodean Bookclub" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/88950688-vicki-antipodean-bookclub"><img alt="Vicki Antipodean Bookclub" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542337038p2/88950688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2962720364?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vicki Antipodean Bookclub" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vicki Antipodean Bookclub" href="/user/show/88950688-vicki-antipodean-bookclub">Vicki Antipodean Bookclub</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007532834" href="/book/show/21088731-when-hitler-stole-pink-rabbit">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2962720364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15157087032046046346">“For a moment she felt terribly sad about Pink Rabbit. It had embroidered black eyes - the original glass ones had fallen out years before - and an endearing habit of collapsing on its paws. Its fur, though no longer very pink, had been soft and familiar. How could she have ever chosen to pack that characterless woolly dog in its stead? It had been a terrible mistake, and now she would never be able to put it right.”<br/>.<br/>.<br/>.<br/>Somehow I managed to get through my childhood never having read When Hitler S</span>
  <span id="freeText15157087032046046346" style="display:none">“For a moment she felt terribly sad about Pink Rabbit. It had embroidered black eyes - the original glass ones had fallen out years before - and an endearing habit of collapsing on its paws. Its fur, though no longer very pink, had been soft and familiar. How could she have ever chosen to pack that characterless woolly dog in its stead? It had been a terrible mistake, and now she would never be able to put it right.”<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />Somehow I managed to get through my childhood never having read When Hitler Stole Pink Rabbit. I listened to an episode of the @bbcworldbookclub podcast where Judith Kerr was becoming increasingly irritated by people’s insistence on making pink rabbit a symbol of her “lost childhood.” Her retort, “Sometimes it’s just a rabbit,” made me laugh and reach for this semi-autobiographical account of Anna and her family who leave Germany just prior to the Nazis coming to power in 1933. They escape to Switzerland, France and then finally to England. Pink Rabbit does what only the very best of children’s literature can do, making a challenging subject accessible and understandable for younger readers. However, there is nuance and depth enough to capture adult readers who can relate to Anna’s parents perhaps more than to Anna or Max her brother. Where Anna sees her mother squeezing her handbag tightly going over the German border, we see a terrified mother of two young children trying to escape. When her father is gently stoking Onkle Julius’ watch with one finger, we see a grieving man whose brother has committed suicide in the face of Nazi persecution. Judith Kerr’s writing has a clarity and simplicity that belies its emotional impact and appeals to readers of all ages. I’m now on the hunt for the next two novels of the trilogy; Bombs on Aunt Daisy and A Small Person Far Away. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15157087032046046346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_461685742" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/461685742" />
    <a title="Louise / Daisy May Johnson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5230131-louise-daisy-may-johnson"><img alt="Louise / Daisy May Johnson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554735943p2/5230131.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/461685742?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Louise / Daisy May Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Louise / Daisy May Johnson" href="/user/show/5230131-louise-daisy-may-johnson">Louise / Daisy May Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5230131-louise-daisy-may-johnson?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5230131-louise-daisy-may-johnson?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5230131-louise-daisy-may-johnson?shelf=war">war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5230131-louise-daisy-may-johnson?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer461685742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9667317653302393035">This book is one of those that feel somehow effortless, as if they were just waiting to be written. Kerr's fictionalised story of her childhood is, and deserves to be, one of those eternal classics of children's literature. <br/><br/>Anna (Judith) is growing up in Germany. She is Jewish, and her father is a famous writer. Following the rise of Nazism, and the climate becoming increasingly fragile in Germany, her parents make the decision to leave. This book follows Anna throughout the first part of her jo</span>
  <span id="freeText9667317653302393035" style="display:none">This book is one of those that feel somehow effortless, as if they were just waiting to be written. Kerr's fictionalised story of her childhood is, and deserves to be, one of those eternal classics of children's literature. <br /><br />Anna (Judith) is growing up in Germany. She is Jewish, and her father is a famous writer. Following the rise of Nazism, and the climate becoming increasingly fragile in Germany, her parents make the decision to leave. This book follows Anna throughout the first part of her journey, from Germany to Switzerland to France and finally to England. The story is then continued in the much darker <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2317701.The_Other_Way_Round__Out_of_the_Hitler_Time___2_" title="The Other Way Round (Out of the Hitler Time, #2) by Judith Kerr" rel="nofollow noopener">The Other Way Round</a>.<br /><br />Anna is young, an innocent in many ways, and we see their journey through her eyes. Kerr's ability is immense in this book, and she delivers the story in a simple, graceful style. It's a quiet book in many parts, reminiscent stylistically of Noel Streatfield's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2531571.A_Vicarage_Family" title="A Vicarage Family by Noel Streatfeild" rel="nofollow noopener">A Vicarage Family</a>, but one that dips into the shadows of imminent war without reservation. There's parts in this book that I remember from my first reading, many years ago, and the impact they had then has not lessened. <br /><br />It's hard not to love the family because of the palpable nature of Kerr's writing. There's a repeated motif of family throughout the book, and the emphatic suggestion that Anna does not mind what happens as long as they are all together. It all adds up to make an idealistic, yet incredibly poignant read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9667317653302393035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_554194363" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kailee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kailee" href="/user/show/12042611-kailee">Kailee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer554194363" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5890193178605981752">This book is about a young girl and her family who move from Germany because they fear Hitler would soon be elected. The story is told from a young girl named Anna’s point of view. It starts off with just her average life; she goes to school, eats dinner with her family, and goes to bed. Her dad decides to move the family, because he is worried that if Hitler is elected that he would take his job away. At the time her dad is a journalist. They end up moving all around Europe.<br/>I didn't enjoy readi</span>
  <span id="freeText5890193178605981752" style="display:none">This book is about a young girl and her family who move from Germany because they fear Hitler would soon be elected. The story is told from a young girl named Anna’s point of view. It starts off with just her average life; she goes to school, eats dinner with her family, and goes to bed. Her dad decides to move the family, because he is worried that if Hitler is elected that he would take his job away. At the time her dad is a journalist. They end up moving all around Europe.<br />I didn't enjoy reading this particular book. There were many things about this book that I did not like. I don't suggest read When Hitler Stole Pink Rabbit. In the beginning I thought that it was going to be good. I thought that the family would get stopped by Hitler when they were leaving the country. Nothing happened. The book was mainly about the family moving and where they lived. I felt like the book didn’t involve Hitler as much as it should have. If the title of the book has Hitler in it then you would think that Hitler is going to be a major role and the pink rabbit was only spoken of once in the book. The only time that the author mentions a pink rabbit was when Anna was trying to decide what stuff animal she wanted to take with her on the move. I also didn’t like the ending. It just left me hanging. The book ending with the family in a new country and they were getting into a cab. I think the author was trying to leave the reader thinking about the rest of their lives, this ending didn’t really satisfy me. I think that a different ending would have been better and would have made a more interesting book overall. <br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2867748651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7168674268321135674">A moving and lovely autobiographical story of Kerr’s refugee childhood. The language is clear as sparkling water; this is beautiful to read. The adult reader is haunted by the allusions woven in. The 10-year-old protagonist does not understand when Uncle Julius says “I have nothing to worry about [in Nazi Germany]; I’m not Jewish, just have this Jewish grandmother.” The adult reader feels a cold shiver run down her spine. The book is full of such moments but at the same time is also full of chil</span>
  <span id="freeText7168674268321135674" style="display:none">A moving and lovely autobiographical story of Kerr’s refugee childhood. The language is clear as sparkling water; this is beautiful to read. The adult reader is haunted by the allusions woven in. The 10-year-old protagonist does not understand when Uncle Julius says “I have nothing to worry about [in Nazi Germany]; I’m not Jewish, just have this Jewish grandmother.” The adult reader feels a cold shiver run down her spine. The book is full of such moments but at the same time is also full of childhood stuff: games and adventure, the challenges of moving to a new school, friends and new clothes. I have myself moved to a new country, a new school and a new language and the vividness with which Kerr describes the experience is wondrous. Her drawings which head up each chapter are also lovely. The 10-year-old girl laments the fact that she will never be famous because she does not have a difficult childhood - to me, the most poignant sentiment here, and a credit to Kerr’s amazing parents who showered their two children with love and a sense of security despite everything. <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="7168674268321135674" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText9913138649495483290" style="display:none">One of the favourite books of my childhood. I used to reread this obsessively, though it's been a long time since I last read it. But I found it a very touching and captivating story of how a child experienced having to flee from country to country after Hitler rose to power in Germany and then also began to overpower other countries. It didn't encumber the storytelling with the sort of historical detail that would have been tiresome to a child, but still gave me a vivid image of what it was like to live in such a time period.</span>

<div id="review_1907283678" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1907283678" />
    <a title="Rebekah Morris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40352095-rebekah-morris"><img alt="Rebekah Morris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467665416p2/40352095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1907283678?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebekah Morris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebekah Morris" href="/user/show/40352095-rebekah-morris">Rebekah Morris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780698115897" href="/book/show/944716.When_Hitler_Stole_Pink_Rabbit">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1907283678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2371419506319162842">Even though this story was written for a younger age, I enjoyed it. It's not often I read a story of a Jewish family who actually left Germany before Hitler got power. The main character is the girl in the story and it gives a new look at life during the beginning of WWII for a refugee family. One think I did find fascinating is that it is a fictional account of the author's own experience of fleeing Germany to escape from the Nazis.<br/>Note: This is not a "Christian" book. There is no praying, chur</span>
  <span id="freeText2371419506319162842" style="display:none">Even though this story was written for a younger age, I enjoyed it. It's not often I read a story of a Jewish family who actually left Germany before Hitler got power. The main character is the girl in the story and it gives a new look at life during the beginning of WWII for a refugee family. One think I did find fascinating is that it is a fictional account of the author's own experience of fleeing Germany to escape from the Nazis.<br />Note: This is not a "Christian" book. There is no praying, church going and the girl once mentions that she doesn't believe there really is a God.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2371419506319162842" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

The writing style is easy to follow and the adventures chronicled included adjusting to different schools and languages as well as hatred.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zVD8rOveTJVF3wLdvvRfx+ys2pgOeB0BDl0QtqXyA7YrAhekyjNk520KcE6l379a6fbbzaByNeP6qEQKKIQc+Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+c80X4V3pXF4T//7hmX2W2wEsjagKyCYwpPjbY7vwDUfnd9XpJqNA1CajWidThbGaV6zYw4hCHo2ZrfRA5nfeg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1150755681297549015">Judith Kerr was a German-born British writer and illustrator who has created both enduring picture books such as the <i>Mog</i> series and <i>The Tiger Who Came To Tea</i> and acclaimed novels for older children such as the autobiographical <i>When Hitler Stole Pink Rabbit</i> which give a child's-eye view of the Second World War.<br/><br/>Kerr was born in Berlin but left Germany with her parents and her brother, Michael, in 19</span>
  <span id="freeText1150755681297549015" style="display:none">Judith Kerr was a German-born British writer and illustrator who has created both enduring picture books such as the <i>Mog</i> series and <i>The Tiger Who Came To Tea</i> and acclaimed novels for older children such as the autobiographical <i>When Hitler Stole Pink Rabbit</i> which give a child's-eye view of the Second World War.<br /><br />Kerr was born in Berlin but left Germany with her parents and her brother, Michael, in 1933, soon after the Nazis first came to power. They were forced to leave as her father, noted drama critic, journalist and screenwriter <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/707248.Alfred_Kerr" title="Alfred Kerr" rel="nofollow noopener">Alfred Kerr</a>, had openly criticised the Nazis,who burned his books shortly after the family had fled Germany. They travelled first to Switzerland and then on into France, before finally settling in Britain, where Kerr has lived ever since. She subsequently became a naturalised British citizen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1150755681297549015" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1877851-when-hitler-stole-pink-rabbit">Quotes from When Hitler Stole...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;We’ll come back,” said Papa.<br />“I know,” said Anna... “But it won’t be the same - we won’t belong. Do you think we’ll ever really belong anywhere?”<br />“I suppose not,” said Papa. “Not the way people belong who have lived in one place all their lives. But we’ll belong a little in lots of places, and I think that may be just as good.&rdquo;</span>
